</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ele2.bustarhymesuniverse.com/">ele2<wbr />.bustarhymesuniverse<wbr />.com</a></span>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Trevor George Smith Jr.</b> (born May 20, 1972), known professionally as <b>Busta Rhymes</b>, is an American rapper, singer, songwriter, record producer and actor. <a href="/wiki/Chuck_D" title="Chuck D">Chuck D</a> of <a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Enemy (band)">Public Enemy</a> gave him the moniker Busta Rhymes, after <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">CFL</a> wide receiver <a href="/wiki/Buster_Rhymes" title="Buster Rhymes">George "Buster" Rhymes</a>. He has received 12 <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nominations for his work, making him <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_records#Most_nominations_without_winning" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award records">one of the most-nominated artists without winning</a>.
</p><p>Busta Rhymes was an original member of <a href="/wiki/Leaders_of_the_New_School" title="Leaders of the New School">Leaders of the New School</a>, a group that attracted national attention when they opened on tour for Public Enemy.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He gained exposure for their guest appearance on <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>'s track "<a href="/wiki/Scenario_(song)" title="Scenario (song)">Scenario</a>". Shortly thereafter, the group broke up, leading Rhymes to become a sought after solo artist, appearing on numerous tracks for other artists before his solo debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Coming" title="The Coming">The Coming</a></i> (1996). The album reached the top ten on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> album chart, was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), and earned him a <a href="/wiki/Grammy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy">Grammy</a> nomination.
</p><p>He has released ten total solo albums, with the most recent being 2020's <i><a href="/wiki/Extinction_Level_Event_2:_The_Wrath_of_God" title="Extinction Level Event 2: The Wrath of God">Extinction Level Event 2: The Wrath of God</a></i>. Rhymes' list of hit singles include "<a href="/wiki/Woo-Hah!!_Got_You_All_in_Check" title="Woo-Hah!! Got You All in Check">Woo-Hah!! Got You All in Check</a>", "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Party_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="It&#39;s a Party (Busta Rhymes song)">It's a Party</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Put_Your_Hands_Where_My_Eyes_Could_See" title="Put Your Hands Where My Eyes Could See">Put Your Hands Where My Eyes Could See</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Dangerous_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="Dangerous (Busta Rhymes song)">Dangerous</a>", <a href="/wiki/Turn_It_Up_(Remix)/Fire_It_Up" class="mw-redirect" title="Turn It Up (Remix)/Fire It Up">"Turn It Up" (Remix)/"Fire It Up"</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_Some_More" title="Gimme Some More">Gimme Some More</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_It_Gonna_Be%3F" class="mw-redirect" title="What&#39;s It Gonna Be?">What's It Gonna Be?</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Pass_the_Courvoisier,_Part_II" title="Pass the Courvoisier, Part II">Pass the Courvoisier, Part II</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Know_What_You_Want" title="I Know What You Want">I Know What You Want</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Touch_It_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="Touch It (Busta Rhymes song)">Touch It</a>".
</p><p>Among his other ventures, he founded the record label <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(record_label)" title="Conglomerate (record label)">Conglomerate</a> (initially Flipmode Entertainment) and the production crew The Conglomerate (formerly Flipmode Squad). <a href="/wiki/About.com" class="mw-redirect" title="About.com">About.com</a> included him on its list of the 50 Greatest <a href="/wiki/Master_of_ceremonies#Hip_hop" title="Master of ceremonies">MCs</a> of Our Time (1987–2007),<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> while Steve Huey of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> called him one of the best and most prolific rappers of the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Source (magazine)">The Source</a></i> placed him on their list of the Top 50 Lyricists of All Time.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> has called him "one of hip-hop's greatest visual artists".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Busta Rhymes was born Trevor George Smith Jr.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/East_Flatbush" class="mw-redirect" title="East Flatbush">East Flatbush</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York City, on May 20, 1972, to Geraldine Green and Trevor Smith Sr., both from Jamaica.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> At age 12, Smith's family moved to <a href="/wiki/Uniondale,_New_York" title="Uniondale, New York">Uniondale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> For a short while, Smith attended <a href="/wiki/George_Westinghouse_Career_and_Technical_Education_High_School" title="George Westinghouse Career and Technical Education High School">George Westinghouse Career and Technical Education High School</a> in Brooklyn with future rappers <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">Christopher "The Notorious B.I.G." Wallace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Shawn "Jay-Z" Carter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and attended <a href="/wiki/Samuel_J._Tilden_High_School" title="Samuel J. Tilden High School">Samuel J. Tilden High School</a> with <a href="/wiki/Special_Ed_(rapper)" title="Special Ed (rapper)">Edward "Special Ed" Archer</a> and Roderick "Chip Fu" Roachford of <a href="/wiki/Fu-Schnickens" title="Fu-Schnickens">Fu-Schnickens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Smith eventually graduated from Long Island's <a href="/wiki/Uniondale_High_School" title="Uniondale High School">Uniondale High School</a> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Busta also spent time in Britain during the early 1980s where he resided with his maternal aunt. She lived in <a href="/wiki/Morecambe" title="Morecambe">Morecambe</a> and he spent two summers there with his mother and younger brother.<sup id="cite_ref-GQ2020_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GQ2020-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He went to <a href="/wiki/Skerton_Community_High_School" title="Skerton Community High School">Skerton Community High School</a> while he was staying in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He told <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> in a 2020 interview, "One summer when we went down there I was 12, my brother was eight, so my aunt made sure that we actually went to school in England. Regular school and then we went to karate school too. We also were on some <a href="/wiki/Breakdancing" title="Breakdancing">breakdancing</a> that was so crazy, we ended up actually getting work to breakdance in clubs as minors. And our cousins used to run us around and they used to advertise us as TJ and Paul."<sup id="cite_ref-GQ2020_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GQ2020-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1986.E2.80.931995:_Leaders_of_the_New_School_and_rising_popularity"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1986–1995:_Leaders_of_the_New_School_and_rising_popularity">1986–1995: Leaders of the New School and rising popularity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1986–1995: Leaders of the New School and rising popularity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Busta_rhymes-06-mika.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Busta_rhymes-06-mika.jpg/170px-Busta_rhymes-06-mika.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Busta_rhymes-06-mika.jpg/255px-Busta_rhymes-06-mika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Busta_rhymes-06-mika.jpg/340px-Busta_rhymes-06-mika.jpg 2x" data-file-width="905" data-file-height="1355" /></a><figcaption>Busta Rhymes in 2002</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1986, Smith, alongside fellow <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> natives Charlie Brown (born Bryan Higgins), Dinco D (born James Jackson) and Cut Monitor Milo (born Sheldon Scott), formed the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_hip_hop" title="East Coast hip hop">East Coast hip hop</a> group <a href="/wiki/Leaders_of_the_New_School" title="Leaders of the New School">Leaders of the New School</a>. The group's big break was when they became an <a href="/wiki/Opening_act" title="Opening act">opening act</a> for hip hop group <a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Enemy (band)">Public Enemy</a>. Public Enemy's <a href="/wiki/Chuck_D" title="Chuck D">Chuck D</a> gave Busta Rhymes and Charlie Brown their respective stage names.<sup id="cite_ref-ALLMUSIC_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALLMUSIC-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Leaders of the New School began recording in late 1990 and released their debut album <i><a href="/wiki/A_Future_Without_a_Past..." title="A Future Without a Past...">A Future Without a Past...</a></i> in 1991 on <a href="/wiki/Elektra_Records" title="Elektra Records">Elektra Records</a>. In early 1992, the group appeared on <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Posse_cut" title="Posse cut">posse cut</a> "<a href="/wiki/Scenario_(song)" title="Scenario (song)">Scenario</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, they released <i><a href="/wiki/T.I.M.E._(The_Inner_Mind%27s_Eye)" title="T.I.M.E. (The Inner Mind&#39;s Eye)">T.I.M.E. (The Inner Mind's Eye)</a></i>. Smith gained popularity from his advanced rhymes as well as his unique style that was not common of many New York rap artists at the time. Raised by two Jamaican parents, Smith embraced his heritage in his music and image as an artist. Smith was the only member of the group to wear dreads and use Jamaican slang, or patois, in his raps. Smith's unique style added an element to the group that allowed for rapid success. Soon after, however, internal problems arose because of his increasing popularity, and the group broke up on the set of <i><a href="/wiki/Yo!_MTV_Raps" title="Yo! MTV Raps">Yo! MTV Raps</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the summer of 1992, Rhymes began making guest appearances on songs by several artists such as <a href="/wiki/Big_Daddy_Kane" title="Big Daddy Kane">Big Daddy Kane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Another_Bad_Creation" title="Another Bad Creation">Another Bad Creation</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brand_Nubian" title="Brand Nubian">Brand Nubian</a>, <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>, and <a href="/wiki/KRS-One" title="KRS-One">KRS-One</a>, as well on the interludes to <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>'s debut <i><a href="/wiki/What%27s_the_411%3F" title="What&#39;s the 411?">What's the 411?</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> trio <a href="/wiki/TLC_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="TLC (band)">TLC</a>'s second album <i><a href="/wiki/CrazySexyCool" title="CrazySexyCool">CrazySexyCool</a></i>. He also appeared on the album jacket of fellow hip-hop group A Tribe Called Quest's <i><a href="/wiki/Midnight_Marauders" title="Midnight Marauders">Midnight Marauders</a></i>, with a host of other fellow hip-hop pioneers. In early 1993, he appeared in a cameo role in <i><a href="/wiki/Who%27s_the_Man%3F" title="Who&#39;s the Man?">Who's the Man?</a></i> with his fellow Leaders of the New School group members. That same year, he appeared as part of an <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">ensemble cast</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Forest_Whitaker" title="Forest Whitaker">Forest Whitaker</a>-directed <i><a href="/wiki/Strapped" title="Strapped">Strapped</a></i> which also starred rapper and actor <a href="/wiki/Fredro_Starr" title="Fredro Starr">Fredro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bokeem_Woodbine" title="Bokeem Woodbine">Bokeem Woodbine</a> and co-starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Ice_Cube" title="Ice Cube">Ice Cube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Omar_Epps" title="Omar Epps">Omar Epps</a> in the <a href="/wiki/John_Singleton" title="John Singleton">John Singleton</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Higher_Learning_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Higher Learning (film)">Higher Learning</a></i>.
</p><p>In mid-1994, Rhymes continued to make guest appearances such as the single "<a href="/wiki/Oh_My_God_(A_Tribe_Called_Quest_song)" title="Oh My God (A Tribe Called Quest song)">Oh My God</a>" with <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>, he teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Puff Daddy</a>, <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rampage_(rapper)" title="Rampage (rapper)">Rampage</a> and former classmate <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>, on a remix to <a href="/wiki/Craig_Mack" title="Craig Mack">Craig Mack</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Flava_in_Ya_Ear" title="Flava in Ya Ear">Flava in Ya Ear</a>", soon after he would team up again with The Notorious B.I.G. with rappers such as <a href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-n-Harmony" title="Bone Thugs-n-Harmony">Bone Thugs-n-Harmony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coolio" title="Coolio">Coolio</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Posse_cut" title="Posse cut">posse cut</a>, "<a href="/wiki/The_Points" title="The Points">The Points</a>" which appeared on <a href="/wiki/Panther_(soundtrack)" class="mw-redirect" title="Panther (soundtrack)">the soundtrack</a> to the 1995 film <i><a href="/wiki/Panther_(film)" title="Panther (film)">Panther</a></i>. At this time, Rhymes engaged in a <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyle</a> battle rap with <a href="/wiki/Ol%27_Dirty_Bastard" title="Ol&#39; Dirty Bastard">Ol' Dirty Bastard</a>, rapping the first few verses of his future breakout debut single "<a href="/wiki/Woo-Hah!!_Got_You_All_in_Check" title="Woo-Hah!! Got You All in Check">Woo-Hah!!</a>" in early 1995. Rhymes also worked on unreleased material with artists such as <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>. Some or neither of the collaborations came to fruition, and Rhymes begun recording what would be <a href="/wiki/The_Coming" title="The Coming">his debut studio album</a> in late 1995.
</p>
<h3><span id="1995.E2.80.931999:_The_Coming.2C_When_Disaster_Strikes.2C_and_Extinction_Level_Event:_The_Final_World_Front"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1995–1999:_The_Coming,_When_Disaster_Strikes,_and_Extinction_Level_Event:_The_Final_World_Front">1995–1999: <i>The Coming</i>, <i>When Disaster Strikes</i>, and <i>Extinction Level Event: The Final World Front</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1995–1999: The Coming, When Disaster Strikes, and Extinction Level Event: The Final World Front">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the summer of 1995, Busta Rhymes began working on his solo debut album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Coming" title="The Coming">The Coming</a></i>, and a month after recording was completed, he released it in March 1996. A month before the album was released, he broke out with a hit single, "<a href="/wiki/Woo_Hah!!_Got_You_All_in_Check" class="mw-redirect" title="Woo Hah!! Got You All in Check">Woo Hah!! Got You All in Check</a>". Later, he started work on his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/When_Disaster_Strikes" class="mw-redirect" title="When Disaster Strikes">When Disaster Strikes</a></i>, which would not be released until September 1997. It produced the hit singles "<a href="/wiki/Put_Your_Hands_Where_My_Eyes_Could_See" title="Put Your Hands Where My Eyes Could See">Put Your Hands Where My Eyes Could See</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Turn_It_Up_(Remix)/Fire_It_Up" class="mw-redirect" title="Turn It Up (Remix)/Fire It Up">Fire It Up</a>". His musical journey saw him become one of the most successful and high net worth rappers in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, Busta Rhymes recorded <i><a href="/wiki/Extinction_Level_Event:_The_Final_World_Front" title="Extinction Level Event: The Final World Front">Extinction Level Event: The Final World Front</a>)</i>. Its lead single "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_Some_More" title="Gimme Some More">Gimme Some More</a>" — which sampled <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Herrmann" title="Bernard Herrmann">Bernard Herrmann</a>'s theme from <i><a href="/wiki/Psycho_(1960_film)" title="Psycho (1960 film)">Psycho</a></i> — reached No. 6 in the UK singles chart in January 1999. Busta Rhymes enjoyed further transatlantic success in April, when the single "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_It_Gonna_Be%3F!" title="What&#39;s It Gonna Be?!">What's It Gonna Be?!</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a>, reached the US and UK Top 11. The album received prominent notice for featuring the fastest <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rapping</a> Busta Rhymes has performed, particularly on a song called "Iz They Wildin Wit Us?", featuring a guest appearance by <a href="/wiki/Mystikal" title="Mystikal">Mystikal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ALLMUSIC-2_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALLMUSIC-2-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>That same year, the Flipmode Squad released <a href="/wiki/The_Imperial_(Flipmode_Squad_album)" title="The Imperial (Flipmode Squad album)">their group album</a>, and from there, they continued to collaborate.
</p>
<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932004:_Anarchy.2C_Genesis.2C_and_It_Ain.27t_Safe_No_More"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000–2004:_Anarchy,_Genesis,_and_It_Ain't_Safe_No_More">2000–2004: <i>Anarchy</i>, <i>Genesis</i>, and <i>It Ain't Safe No More</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2000–2004: Anarchy, Genesis, and It Ain&#039;t Safe No More">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Busta_rhymes_breaks_it_down_for_the_mobile_geeks.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Busta_rhymes_breaks_it_down_for_the_mobile_geeks.jpg/220px-Busta_rhymes_breaks_it_down_for_the_mobile_geeks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Busta_rhymes_breaks_it_down_for_the_mobile_geeks.jpg/330px-Busta_rhymes_breaks_it_down_for_the_mobile_geeks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Busta_rhymes_breaks_it_down_for_the_mobile_geeks.jpg/440px-Busta_rhymes_breaks_it_down_for_the_mobile_geeks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360" /></a><figcaption>Busta Rhymes performing in 2006</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Flipmode_Squad" title="Flipmode Squad">Flipmode Squad</a></div>
<p>In 2000, Busta Rhymes recorded his final album for Elektra, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Anarchy_(Busta_Rhymes_album)" title="Anarchy (Busta Rhymes album)">Anarchy</a></i>. After Busta signed to <a href="/wiki/J_Records" title="J Records">J Records</a>, a label started by the then recently ousted <a href="/wiki/Arista_Records" title="Arista Records">Arista Records</a> chief and founder <a href="/wiki/Clive_Davis" title="Clive Davis">Clive Davis</a>, he released a greatest hits collection <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Devastation:_The_Best_of_Busta_Rhymes" title="Total Devastation: The Best of Busta Rhymes">Total Devastation: The Best of Busta Rhymes</a></i>, alongside a new album of original work. Continuing the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Biblical</a> theme of his previous albums, he titled his record <i><a href="/wiki/Genesis_(Busta_Rhymes_album)" title="Genesis (Busta Rhymes album)">Genesis</a></i>. The album featured collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, <a href="/wiki/P._Diddy" class="mw-redirect" title="P. Diddy">P. Diddy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelis" title="Kelis">Kelis</a>, and others. Genesis was powered by the hit single with Kelis, "What It Is", and his solo single released in November 2001, "<a href="/wiki/Break_Ya_Neck" title="Break Ya Neck">Break Ya Neck</a>". The final single was the summer smash "<a href="/wiki/Pass_the_Courvoisier,_Part_II" title="Pass the Courvoisier, Part II">Pass the Courvoisier, Part II</a>", which featured <a href="/wiki/Pharrell" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharrell">Pharrell</a> and P. Diddy. Despite the success of the two singles, this album did not sell as well as previous releases. Fellow Flipmode members were featured, but minor changes in the roster were noted.
</p><p>In 2002, Busta Rhymes released his sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/It_Ain%27t_Safe_No_More" class="mw-redirect" title="It Ain&#39;t Safe No More">It Ain't Safe No More</a></i>. The album was moderately successful, with a hit song featuring <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> and the Flipmode Squad titled "<a href="/wiki/I_Know_What_You_Want" title="I Know What You Want">I Know What You Want</a>". Another hit single was "<a href="/wiki/Make_It_Clap" title="Make It Clap">Make It Clap</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Spliff_Star" title="Spliff Star">Spliff Star</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remix</a> of "Make It Clap", features <a href="/wiki/Sean_Paul" title="Sean Paul">Sean Paul</a>. After its release, Busta Rhymes left <a href="/wiki/J_Records" title="J Records">J Records</a>. In 2004, he signed with American record producer and record executive <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>. Consequently, upon changing label, a new Flipmode album was cancelled and shelved. As a side note, Busta was also featured as a playable fighter in the 2004 fighting game <i><a href="/wiki/Def_Jam:_Fight_For_NY" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Jam: Fight For NY">Def Jam: Fight For NY</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2005.E2.80.932009:_The_Big_Bang_and_Back_on_My_B.S."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005–2009:_The_Big_Bang_and_Back_on_My_B.S.">2005–2009: <i>The Big Bang</i> and <i>Back on My B.S.</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2005–2009: The Big Bang and Back on My B.S.">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>His seventh studio album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_(Busta_Rhymes_album)" title="The Big Bang (Busta Rhymes album)">The Big Bang</a></i>, became the first No. 1 album of his career. The album sold over 209,000 copies in its first week to earn the top spot on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The album also became his highest-charting album in the UK, peaking at No. 19. Some of the album was previously <a href="/wiki/Music_leak" title="Music leak">leaked online</a>, and as a result several songs were left off the album and new ones added. <i>The Big Bang</i> features production by Dr. Dre and <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>, as well as appearances by <a href="/wiki/Raekwon" title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>. The album spawned the singles "<a href="/wiki/Touch_It_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="Touch It (Busta Rhymes song)">Touch It</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Love_My_Bitch" title="I Love My Bitch">I Love My Bitch</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Kelis" title="Kelis">Kelis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>, "<a href="/wiki/New_York_Shit" title="New York Shit">New York Shit</a>", featuring Swizz Beatz and "<a href="/wiki/In_the_Ghetto_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="In the Ghetto (Busta Rhymes song)">In The Ghetto</a>". Busta Rhymes also had a stint opening for <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Mimi_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="The Adventures of Mimi Tour">The Adventures of Mimi Tour</a>. Also, he has performed with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> on "Touch It Remix Part 5" and who also performed a verse on the aforementioned rapper's song, "I'll Hurt You". On July 17, 2008, Busta left Interscope and Aftermath due to a creative clash with Interscope head <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a>.
</p><p>In 2007, Busta Rhymes released the song "<a href="/wiki/We_Made_It_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="We Made It (song)">We Made It</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>. He also made an original song, "Where's My Money", for a fictional radio station in the 2008 video game <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_IV" title="Grand Theft Auto IV">Grand Theft Auto IV</a></i>. It was later revealed that Busta signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Universal_Motown" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Motown">Universal Motown</a>, through which he released his eighth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Back_on_My_B.S." title="Back on My B.S.">Back on My B.S.</a></i>, on May 19, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-universalmotown_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-universalmotown-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at No. 5 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200. The album was supported by the singles "<a href="/wiki/Arab_Money" title="Arab Money">Arab Money</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Ron_Browz" title="Ron Browz">Ron Browz</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Hustler%27s_Anthem_%2709" title="Hustler&#39;s Anthem &#39;09">Hustler's Anthem '09</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/T-Pain" title="T-Pain">T-Pain</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Respect_My_Conglomerate" title="Respect My Conglomerate">Respect My Conglomerate</a>". The song "<a href="/wiki/World_Go_Round" title="World Go Round">World Go Round</a>", featuring British singer <a href="/wiki/Estelle_(musician)" title="Estelle (musician)">Estelle</a>, was released in France on April 6, 2009, due to the heavy rotation of a leaked version. The single was released in the UK on July 13, 2009. Busta Rhymes also appeared on <a href="/wiki/Asher_Roth" title="Asher Roth">Asher Roth</a>'s debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Asleep_in_the_Bread_Aisle" title="Asleep in the Bread Aisle">Asleep in the Bread Aisle</a></i>.
</p><p>Due to controversial content, the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> (UAE) has banned the album. <i>Back on My B.S.</i> was released internationally, but because of one song, "<a href="/wiki/Arab_Money" title="Arab Money">Arab Money</a>", it cannot be purchased as a CD there, although the album can still be purchased via <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>. According to the National Media Council, the lyrics were considered to be offensive to Arabs and to Islam, because it quoted the <a href="/wiki/Shahada" title="Shahada">Shahada</a>.
</p><p>In November 2008, when "Arab Money" was released as a single, DJ Dany Neville and the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi people">Iraqi</a> rapper The Narcicyst responded by recording a reply. Rhymes later apologized. DJs in the country said they had not received an order banning the record from being spun in nightclubs, and they had mixed feelings on whether the record was offensive or not.<sup id="cite_ref-thenational.ae_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenational.ae-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> DJ Saif of <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> said, "I don't play 'Arab Money' because it's disrespectful [to] Arabs. I don't think there is a ban on playing it in clubs, but many here don't play it anyway."<sup id="cite_ref-thenational.ae_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenational.ae-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Busta_rhymes-03-mika.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Busta_rhymes-03-mika.jpg/220px-Busta_rhymes-03-mika.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Busta_rhymes-03-mika.jpg/330px-Busta_rhymes-03-mika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Busta_rhymes-03-mika.jpg/440px-Busta_rhymes-03-mika.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1356" data-file-height="905" /></a><figcaption>Busta Rhymes in 2005</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/DJ_Bliss" title="DJ Bliss">DJ Bliss</a>, along with many other DJs in the UAE, refused to play "Arab Money" on Radio 1 in Dubai after it was banned in the UAE for offense to Arabs. He added, "I used to play the original version in the club, but out of respect for the laws here in my country, I haven't played it since."<sup id="cite_ref-thenational.ae_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenational.ae-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 the track's producer <a href="/wiki/Ron_Browz" title="Ron Browz">Ron Browz</a> defended Busta Rhymes in a Dubai interview with journalist Awad Mustafa stating that the track was misunderstood.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> "For us, having 'Arab money' is a compliment understood like having 'Oprah money' or 'Tiger Woods money' – it's just street slang, and we were appreciating the amazing wonders that have been created here," Browz said.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Browz added that he had produced the track in a moment of inspiration while experimenting in his studio. "Growing up in Harlem I was always surrounded by Arabs and <a href="/wiki/Islam_and_Hip-Hop_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Islam and Hip-Hop in the United States">Muslims</a>, we embraced their culture and they embraced ours and we always joked with each other," he said.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.93present:_Collaborations_and_Extinction_Level_Event_2"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–present:_Collaborations_and_Extinction_Level_Event_2">2010–present: Collaborations and <i>Extinction Level Event 2</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010–present: Collaborations and Extinction Level Event 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 2009, Busta Rhymes had announced that he was working on his ninth studio album, alongside Canadian producer <a href="/wiki/Boi-1da" title="Boi-1da">Boi-1da</a>, entitled <i>The Chemo</i>. At the time, he stated that the project was 80% finished.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In May 2010, Busta Rhymes had reportedly changed the title of his ninth album from <i>The Chemo</i> to <i>Extinction Level Event 2</i>, making his ninth effort a sequel to his 1998 album <i>Extinction Level Event (Final World Front)</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an August 6, 2010 interview on Conspiracy Worldwide Radio, American hip hop producer <a href="/wiki/DJ_Premier" title="DJ Premier">DJ Premier</a> said Busta Rhymes received over eight beats which he did not want to use but Premier hoped his next beat would be chosen for inclusion on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On DJ Premier's Live from Headqcourterz radio show, Premier confirmed that one of his beats were to be included in <i>E.L.E. 2</i>. In 2010, Busta Rhymes formed his new label, The Conglomerate Entertainment (later on, the label would have artists such as <a href="/wiki/N.O.R.E." title="N.O.R.E.">N.O.R.E.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spliff_Star" title="Spliff Star">Spliff Star</a> on its roster). He was also featured on "C'mon (Catch 'Em By Surprise)" by <a href="/wiki/Ti%C3%ABsto" title="Tiësto">Tiësto</a> and Diplo.
</p><p>In 2011, Rhymes recorded "<a href="/wiki/Look_at_Me_Now_(Chris_Brown_song)" title="Look at Me Now (Chris Brown song)">Look at Me Now</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> on Brown's fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/F.A.M.E._(Chris_Brown_album)" title="F.A.M.E. (Chris Brown album)">F.A.M.E.</a></i>; the song received favorable reviews regarding Rhymes guest verse on the song, and is his highest chart entry on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, peaking at No. 6, while reaching No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart, becoming his first No. 1 on that chart. On September 7, 2011, Rhymes received six nominations for the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>, held on October 11, 2011.
</p><p>On May 1, 2011, Rhymes appeared on the launch show for MNET's <i>Big Brother Africa 6: Amplified</i> and performed some of his songs. In 2011, Busta Rhymes performed at the <a href="/wiki/Gathering_of_the_Juggalos" title="Gathering of the Juggalos">Gathering of the Juggalos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Busta Rhymes contributed to the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Tech_N9ne" title="Tech N9ne">Tech N9ne</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/All_6%27s_and_7%27s" title="All 6&#39;s and 7&#39;s">All 6's and 7's</a></i>, performing vocals on the single, "Worldwide Choppers", released on May 31.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Canadian recording artist <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a> featured Busta Rhymes on a song called "Drummer Boy" off Bieber's sophomore studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Under_the_Mistletoe" title="Under the Mistletoe">Under the Mistletoe</a></i>, released on November 1, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On November 11, 2011, a <a href="/wiki/Heavy_D" title="Heavy D">Heavy D</a> tribute song titled "You Ain't Gotta Wait Till I'm Gone" was leaked.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 16, 2011, it was announced that Busta Rhymes signed to <a href="/wiki/Cash_Money_Records" title="Cash Money Records">Cash Money Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> For his debut single on the Cash Money label and his Conglomerate Records, he reunited with <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a> on the single "<a href="/wiki/Why_Stop_Now_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="Why Stop Now (Busta Rhymes song)">Why Stop Now</a>". In 2012, Busta collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Jodie_Connor" title="Jodie Connor">Jodie Connor</a>, featuring on her single "Take You There", but he did not appear in the music video.
</p><p>A song with Twista, titled "Can You Keep Up", was leaked. Busta Rhymes was featured on <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a>'s single "Pride &amp; Joy" alongside <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> His ninth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Year_of_the_Dragon_(Busta_Rhymes_album)" title="Year of the Dragon (Busta Rhymes album)">Year of the Dragon</a></i>, was released for free on <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a> on August 21, 2012. The album features guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trey_Songz" title="Trey Songz">Trey Songz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Thicke" title="Robin Thicke">Robin Thicke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maino_(rapper)" title="Maino (rapper)">Maino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gucci_Mane" title="Gucci Mane">Gucci Mane</a> and more. He also released a music video for the track "Doin' It Again" which features <a href="/wiki/Reek_da_Villian" title="Reek da Villian">Reek da Villian</a> and includes a tribute to his manager, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Lighty" title="Chris Lighty">Chris Lighty</a>, who committed suicide in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was later featured on YMCMB label mate Shannel's single "Last Time".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, it was announced that Universal Motown was going defunct, forcing Rhymes and other artists to move to <a href="/wiki/Universal_Republic_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Republic Records">Universal Republic Records</a>. In mid-2012, it was announced that Universal Republic Records was also going defunct, forcing artists on the roster to move to <a href="/wiki/Republic_Records" title="Republic Records">Republic Records</a>, reviving the label.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 21, 2012, members of The Conglomerate Ent., Busta along with J. Doe and Reek da Villan released a mixtape titled <i>Catastrophic</i>, their first collective effort.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Busta Rhymes collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a>, who produced the first single off his Cash Money Records debut, "<a href="/wiki/Twerk_It" title="Twerk It">Twerk It</a>", which was released June 6, 2013. A video was shot in <a href="/wiki/Flatbush,_Brooklyn" title="Flatbush, Brooklyn">Flatbush</a> on June 3, 2013. The official remix was released featuring <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>. On July 23, 2014, Busta Rhymes announced that he left Cash Money Records due to creative differences and he is no longer on Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On November 7, 2013, he released "<a href="/wiki/Thank_You_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="Thank You (Busta Rhymes song)">Thank You</a>", a song featuring Q-Tip, Kanye West and Lil Wayne.
</p><p>He was featured on "Devil", featuring <a href="/wiki/Neon_Hitch" title="Neon Hitch">Neon Hitch</a> and <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, a song by <a href="/wiki/Cash_Cash" title="Cash Cash">Cash Cash</a>. It was released in August 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In July 2014, it was announced that Rhymes had amicably departed Cash Records due to creative differences.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Out4Fame-Festival_2015_-_Busta_Rhymes_-_2.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Out4Fame-Festival_2015_-_Busta_Rhymes_-_2.JPG/220px-Out4Fame-Festival_2015_-_Busta_Rhymes_-_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Out4Fame-Festival_2015_-_Busta_Rhymes_-_2.JPG/330px-Out4Fame-Festival_2015_-_Busta_Rhymes_-_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Out4Fame-Festival_2015_-_Busta_Rhymes_-_2.JPG/440px-Out4Fame-Festival_2015_-_Busta_Rhymes_-_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a><figcaption>Busta Rhymes at Out4Fame Festival 2015 in Germany</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2016, a movement to name a small, uninhabited lake island in Shrewsbury, Massachusetts after Busta Rhymes received viral publicity. The unofficial name of <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes_Island" title="Busta Rhymes Island">Busta Rhymes Island</a> was chosen by a town resident because the island has "rope-swinging, blueberries, and ... stuff Busta would enjoy".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> A formal proposal was made to the U.S. Board on Geographic Names to officially change the island's name, but it was not accepted due to regulations regarding the naming of geographic places after living people.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Busta Rhymes was also a featured artist on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hamilton_Mixtape" title="The Hamilton Mixtape">The Hamilton Mixtape</a></i>, singing a remix of "<a href="/wiki/My_Shot" title="My Shot">My Shot</a>", along with <a href="/wiki/Black_Thought" title="Black Thought">Black Thought</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joell_Ortiz" title="Joell Ortiz">Joell Ortiz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The trio performed the song on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On February 2, 2018, Rhymes released a new single "Get It", featuring <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Rowland" title="Kelly Rowland">Kelly Rowland</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, he was announced to be a featured artist on Azealia Banks’ album <i><a href="/wiki/Fantasea_II:_The_Second_Wave" class="mw-redirect" title="Fantasea II: The Second Wave">Fantasea II: The Second Wave</a></i>, on the song "Tastes State".
</p><p>In February 2019, Busta Rhymes confirmed he's "finishing touches" of his new album with longtime collaborator, Dr. Dre.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Busta appeared on <a href="/wiki/The_Masked_Singer_(American_season_4)" title="The Masked Singer (American season 4)">season 4</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Masked_Singer_(American_TV_series)" title="The Masked Singer (American TV series)">The Masked Singer</a></i> as the "Dragon". He was eliminated in the first episode.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 30, 2020, Busta released his album <i><a href="/wiki/Extinction_Level_Event_2:_The_Wrath_of_God" title="Extinction Level Event 2: The Wrath of God">Extinction Level Event 2: The Wrath of God</a></i>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(musician)" title="Q-Tip (musician)">Q-Tip</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M.O.P." title="M.O.P.">M.O.P.</a>, among others.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Busta Rhymes identifies as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Five-Percent_Nation" title="Five-Percent Nation">Five-Percent Nation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> He has six children: three sons (born in 1993, 1999, and 2001) and three daughters (born 1998, 1999, and 2006).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During an interview for <a href="/wiki/Hip-Hop:_Beyond_Beats_and_Rhymes" title="Hip-Hop: Beyond Beats and Rhymes">Hip-Hop: Beyond Beats and Rhymes</a>, the rapper walked out when confronted with a question about <a href="/wiki/LGBT_representations_in_hip_hop_music" title="LGBT representations in hip hop music">homophobia in the rap community</a>. Rhymes is quoted as saying: "I can't partake in that conversation," followed by, "With all due respect, I ain't trying to offend nobody. . . We don't support abomination or un-natural stuff." When asked if the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_(culture)" title="Hip hop (culture)">hip hop culture</a> would ever accept a homosexual rapper, Busta Rhymes then exited the interview.<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost1_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost1-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a later interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a>, Busta Rhymes believes marriage is between a Men and Women.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In December 1998, Rhymes was arrested and charged with possession of an unregistered gun after being pulled over during a routine traffic stop in New York City. In October 6, 2000, he received five years probation after pleading guilty earlier in the year.
</p><p>On August 20, 2006, Rhymes was arrested and arraigned for charges of third-degree assault after attacking a man who reportedly spat on his car in New York City on August 12 after the <a href="/wiki/AmsterJam" title="AmsterJam">AmsterJam</a> Music Festival on <a href="/wiki/Randall%27s_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Randall&#39;s Island">Randall's Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 24, 2006, Rhymes appeared at <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> Criminal Court as the <a href="/wiki/District_attorney" title="District attorney">district attorney</a>'s office attempted to amend previous charges against him to include weapons possession for a <a href="/wiki/Machete" title="Machete">machete</a> found in his car. The judge refused to add the charge and adjourned the case.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes1_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes1-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BostonHerald1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonHerald1-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 20, 2007, Rhymes refused a plea deal offered by the prosecutor's office for the assault of his former driver, Edward Hatchett.  The deal would have entailed six months in jail and <a href="/wiki/Guilty_plea" class="mw-redirect" title="Guilty plea">pleading guilty</a> to two assaults, the attack on Hatchett, and the attack on the former fan. The dispute with Hatchett is believed to have originated over back pay Hatchett felt he was owed. Manhattan Criminal Court Judge Becki Rowe offered Busta another option, pleading guilty to third-degree assault. The conditions of the proposed sentence would include five days of <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a>, two weeks of youth lectures and six months of anger management classes, as well as three years of <a href="/wiki/Probation" title="Probation">probation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BostonHerald1_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BostonHerald1-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CourtTV1_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CourtTV1-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 3, 2007, Rhymes was arrested in Manhattan for driving without a license and for driving while impaired. On March 18, 2008, a judge in New York City sentenced Rhymes to three years of probation, 10 days <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a>, $1250 in fines (plus court costs), and to enroll in a drunken driving program.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 25, 2008, Rhymes was temporarily refused entry to the UK due to "unresolved convictions".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018 Busta Rhymes was accused of plagiarism by Bernardo Lanzetti and his group, <a href="/wiki/Acqua_Fragile" title="Acqua Fragile">Acqua Fragile</a>, because in ''Genesis'', the song that gives the title to his 2001 album, he used a sample of ''Cosmic mind affair'', taken from ''Mass Media Stars'', the group's second album, without declaring it and indeed signing it in his own name.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Lanzetti and the group decide to continue the cause;<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> the usage of the sample is approximately 20.09 seconds and is repeated 4 times within Genesis for a usage percentage of approximately 35% of the total duration of the song.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, the name of the original producer of Cosmic mind affair, Claudio Fabi, also disappears from the rapper's album, because J Dilla is listed in this role in the credits.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Since after years of negotiations the situation was not resolved with recognition, Lanzetti and the band decided to take legal action<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Busta Rhymes' favorite rapper as a teenager was <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>, who was the inspiration and reason for Busta Rhymes writing his first raps.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rhymes' work has directly influenced artists such as <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Talib_Kweli_inspiration,_interview_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Talib_Kweli_inspiration,_interview-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ski_Mask_the_Slump_God" title="Ski Mask the Slump God">Ski Mask the Slump God</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Doja_Cat" title="Doja Cat">Doja Cat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Big_Daddy_Kane" title="Big Daddy Kane">Big Daddy Kane</a> has stated that Rhymes has the best flow in <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, alluding to the original version of "<a href="/wiki/Turn_It_Up_(Remix)_/_Fire_It_Up#Original_version" title="Turn It Up (Remix) / Fire It Up">Turn It Up</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Fight_For_NY" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Jam Fight For NY">Def Jam Fight For NY</a></i> (2004) as Magic<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Fight_for_NY:_The_Takeover" title="Def Jam Fight for NY: The Takeover">Def Jam Fight for NY: The Takeover</a></i> (2006) as Magic<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_IV:_The_Lost_and_Damned" title="Grand Theft Auto IV: The Lost and Damned">Grand Theft Auto IV: The Lost and Damned</a></i> (2009) as Himself</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Busta_Rhymes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
